To counter the negative message being sent by Victorias Secret, Dear Kate, a New York City-based retailer, created a more positive parody of the image.  Calling on artists, entrepreneurs, business women, and more real women, the underwear company created a photo that is the antithesis of the Perfect Body ad." itemprop="description" name="description"/>

              <h1 class="Font-A-6-110 title W-100" id="article-aft-title-101437719993">
               What the 'Perfect Body' Really Looks Like
              </h1>
              <div class="GridTable Mx-a">
               <div class="D-tbr row-template">
                <div class="GridTable-Cell Va-t col-left" style="width:800px;min-width:800px;">
                 <div class="content">
                  <img class="Maw-100 Mah-100 Maw-100 Mb-20" src="https://s.yimg.com/cd/resizer/2.0/FIT_TO_WIDTH-w800/b0a3e185893acfdc73e69876cda691e7a5472672.jpg"/>
                  <div class="GridTable grid-content">
                   <div class="D-tbr row-content">
                    <div class="GridTable-Cell Va-t col-left" style="padding-right:20px;">
                     <div class="attribution-component D-b W-100" id="article-aft-attribution-101437719993" style="max-width:280px;">
                      <div class="author-info author-info-text-first Pt-10 W-100 Bd-t Bd-b Bdstart-0 Bdend-0">
                       <div class="GridTable W-100">
                        <div class="D-tbr">
                         <div class="GridTable-Cell Va-t">
                          <cite class="D-b Fs-n Pb-14 byline col">
                           <span class="D-b author-name col-left">
                            <a class="Font-C-2-140 Fw-b" data-action-outcome="navigate" data-routable-url="/style/author/lauren-tuck" data-ylk="t1:a2;t2:article;t3:cat;t8:0c7b2f04-7cfc-3f2f-b4a3-a4c924245f70;t9:16;elm:itm;elmt:cat;itc:0" href="/style/author/lauren-tuck" rel="author" style="color:#000;">
                             Lauren Tuck
                            </a>
                           </span>
                           <span class="D-b Font-C-2-140 Fw-n author-title">
                            News Editor
                           </span>
                           <time class="D-b Font-C-2-140 Fw-n date">
                            <span>
                             October 31, 2014
                            </span>
                           </time>
                           <div class="follow Mt-4">
                            <iframe allowtransparency="true" frameborder="0" scrolling="no" src="//platform.twitter.com/widgets/follow_button.html?screen_name=LTnumberone&amp;show_screen_name=false&amp;show_count=false" style="border:none;overflow:hidden;width:60px;height:20px;">
                            </iframe>
                           </div>
                          </cite>
                         </div>
                        </div>
                       </div>
                      </div>
                     </div>
                    </div>
                    <div class="GridTable-Cell Va-t col-right">
                     <div class="text-body-wrapper W-100 Font-B-1-160">
                      <noscript>
                      </noscript>
                      <div class="text-body W-100 Font-B-1-160" id="article-aft-text-body-101437719993" style="color:#222222;max-width:500px;">
                       <div class="body read-more-cut">
                        <div class="pre-cut" style="height:auto;margin-bottom:1.5em;">
                         <p>
                          In response to a
                          <a data-ylk="elm:itm;elmt:link;t1:a2;t2:article;t3:body;t8:0c7b2f04-7cfc-3f2f-b4a3-a4c924245f70;t9:18;itc:0" href="https://www.yahoo.com/style/victorias-secret-is-sending-mixed-messages-the-101266136378.html" target="_blank">
                           Victorias Secret advertisement
                          </a>
                          that seemed to declare what a perfect body is many reacted strongly calling the campaign irresponsible and harmful. Three students in the U.K. even started a
                          <a data-ylk="elm:itm;elmt:link;t1:a2;t2:article;t3:body;t8:0c7b2f04-7cfc-3f2f-b4a3-a4c924245f70;t9:18;itc:0" href="http://www.change.org/p/victoriassecret-apologise-for-your-damaging-perfect-body-campaign-iamperfect" target="_blank">
                           Change.org petition
                          </a>
                          that, to date, has received more than 15,000 signatures and started a hashtag movement with
                          <span>
                          </span>
                          #iamperfect to promote a different, healthier outlook on body image.
                         </p>
                         <p>
                          <span>
                           To counter the negative message being sent by Victorias Secret, Dear Kate, a New York City-based retailer, created a more positive parody of the image. Calling on artists, entrepreneurs, business women, and more real women, the underwear company created a photo that is the antithesis of the Perfect Body ad. 
                          </span>
                          Through this photo, we showcase women who are often neglected by the media and traditional retailers, a
                          <a data-ylk="elm:itm;elmt:link;t1:a2;t2:article;t3:body;t8:0c7b2f04-7cfc-3f2f-b4a3-a4c924245f70;t9:18;itc:0" href="http://www.dearkates.com/blogs/diary/15637197-the-perfect-body" target="_blank">
                           blog post on the companys website says
                          </a>
                          . We show the multitude of shapes perfect bodies
                          <span>
                          </span>
                          can take.
                          <span>
                          </span>
                         </p>
                         <p>
                          Julie Sygiel, the founder and CEO of Dear Kate, tells Yahoo Style that when the employees of the company say the Perfect Body ad they were collectively shocked
                          <span>
                           that anyone would put something out there that says what the ideal figure is. 
                          </span>
                          <span>
                           I feel like this is very irresponsible and a very damaging message to s. nd and so I wanted to stand up and give another version of what that picture could look like and we wanted to represent as many different shapes as possible, she says.
                          </span>
                         </p>
                         <p>
                          <span>
                           Dear Kate says their message and products are the complete opposite of Victorias Secret. All of their underwear is made with a patent-pending fabric and protects like a pantie liner. Calling the lingerie the 
                          </span>
                          <span>
                           ultimate underwear for women, Sygiel says that its 
                          </span>
                          <span>
                           so much more than a pretty pair of underwear.
                          </span>
                          <span>
                          </span>
                          <span>
                          </span>
                         </p>
                         <p>
                          <span>
                           Sending out a mass email to her entire address book, hundreds of people responded to Sygiel and the company chose a diverse group of women in different h
                          </span>
                          <span>
                           eights, weights, and skin color. The response to the photo has been powerful. Kate Upton and Shonda Rhimes both posted the image to their social media channels and Sygiel has received personal emails from people who have been moved. One commenter said they started crying when they laid eyes on the image and another I
                          </span>
                          <span>
                           ve felt so much pressure and hatred towards my body and I saw this and realized that I am beautiful the way I am.
                          </span>
                          <span>
                          </span>
                         </p>
                        </div>
                        <div class="post-cut W-100" id="post-cut" style="transition-property:none;-webkit-transition-property:none;transition-duration:10s;-webkit-transition-duration:10s;transition-timing-function:ease-in;-webkit-transition-timing-function:ease-in;overflow:hidden;max-height:999999px;max-width:500px;">
                        </div>
                       </div>
                      </div>
                     </div>

Dunham Tries to Cement Her Guru Status","summary":"By Jessica Roy The Lena Dunham experience is getting another brand extension: Starting in September, Dunham will add newsletter publisher to her rsum, right above Emmy-nominated TV producer and Taylor Swift bestie. Along with Girls showrunner Jenni Konner, Dunham plans to launch Lenny, a weekly email newsletter that will offer advice, essays, and product recommendations to millennial women.  Lenny is your over sharing Internet friend who will yell at you about your finances, help you choose a bathing suit, lamp, president  AND tell you what to do if you need an abortion, reads the newsletters mission statement.  Related: 25 Famous Women on Female Friendship Under the direction of Jessica Grose (a veteran of Slate and Jezebel), Lenny will publish a collection of voices on everything from politics to relationships to fashion, aimed at women ages 18 to 34.  Dunham and Konner are funding the newsletter themselves, and the team will start small  along with Grose, the Lenny employees will be Benjamin Cooley (CEO), Laia Garcia (associate editor), and Doreen St. Flix (editor at large)  but will also solicit paid contributions from outside writers.","body":"\u003Cfigure class=\"tmblr-full\"\u003E\n \u003Cimg src=\"https:\u002F\u002Fs.yimg.com\u002Fcd\u002Fdiminuendo\u002F1.0\u002Foriginal\u002F93e528e8e5bff87d374e73f5e61db917f9c522bf.gif\" width=\"400\" height=\"225\" alt=\"Lena Dunham Tries to Cement Her Guru Status\"\u003E\n\u003C\u002Ffigure\u003E\n\u003Cp\u003E\u003Ci\u003EBy \u003Ca href=\"http:\u002F\u002Fnymag.com\u002Fauthor\u002FJessica%20Roy\u002F\"\u003EJessica Roy\u003C\u002Fa\u003E\u003C\u002Fi\u003E\u003Cbr\u003E\u003C\u002Fp\u003E\n\u003Cp\u003EThe Lena Dunham experience is getting another brand extension: Starting in September, Dunham will add &#x201C;newsletter publisher&#x201D; to her r&#xE9;sum&#xE9;, right above &#x201C;Emmy-nominated TV producer&#x201D; and &#x201C;Taylor Swift bestie.&#x201D; Along with \u003Ci\u003EGirls \u003C\u002Fi\u003Eshowrunner Jenni Konner, Dunham plans to launch \u003Ca href=\"http:\u002F\u002Flennyletter.com\u002F\"\u003ELenny\u003C\u002Fa\u003E, a weekly email newsletter that will offer advice, essays, and product recommendations to millennial women. &#x201C;Lenny is your over sharing Internet friend who will yell at you about your finances, help you choose a bathing suit, lamp, president &#x2026; AND tell you what to do if you need an abortion,&#x201D; reads the newsletter&#x2019;s mission statement. \u003Cbr\u003E\u003C\u002Fp\u003E\n\u003Cp\u003E\u003Cb\u003E\u003Ci\u003ERelated:\u003C\u002Fi\u003E \u003Ca href=\"http:\u002F\u002Fnymag.com\u002Fthecut\u002F2015\u002F04\u002F25-famous-women-on-female-friendship.html?mid=yahoostyle\"\u003E\u003Ci\u003E25 Famous Women on Female Friendship\u003C\u002Fi\u003E\u003C\u002Fa\u003E\u003C\u002Fb\u003E\u003Cbr\u003E\u003C\u002Fp\u003E\n\u003Cp\u003EUnder the direction of Jessica Grose (a veteran of Slate and Jezebel), Lenny will publish a collection of voices on everything from politics to relationships to fashion, aimed at women ages 18 to 34. Dunham and Konner are funding the newsletter themselves, and the team will start small &#x2014; along with Grose, the Lenny employees will be Benjamin Cooley (CEO), Laia Garcia (associate editor), and Doreen St. F&#xE9;lix (editor at large) &#x2014; but will also solicit paid contributions from outside writers. Audrey Gelman will serve as an outside adviser. Eventually, they plan to expand into e-commerce, focusing on artisan products created by women.\u003C\u002Fp\u003E\n\u003Cp\u003EDunham told the Cut she came up with the idea for Lenny on the tour for her book, \u003Ci\u003ENot That Kind of Girl\u003C\u002Fi\u003E, during which she met hundreds of young women who were &#x201C;inspiring me with their sense of community and their deep, deep desire for intelligent, politically liberal, thoughtful content that would speak to them.&#x201D; Dunham and Konner saw a newsletter as the ideal incarnation of that editorial space: a place where they could expand beyond Twitter&#x2019;s character limit but also not feel burdened by daily updates. Plus, Grose added, &#x201C;a newsletter seemed like the perfect opportunity to grow, but it doesn&#x2019;t have this pressure of pageviews.&#x201D;\u003C\u002Fp\u003E\n\u003Cp\u003EThe newsletter plans to target an audience that is more diverse than, say, the first-season cast of \u003Ci\u003EGirls \u003C\u002Fi\u003E&#x2014; it won&#x2019;t just be for &#x201C;straight, white cisgender women,&#x201D; Dunham told the Cut.\u003C\u002Fp\u003E\n\u003Cp\u003E\u003Cb\u003E\u003Ci\u003ERelated:\u003C\u002Fi\u003E \u003Ca href=\"http:\u002F\u002Fnymag.com\u002Fthecut\u002F2014\u002F03\u002Fsee-lena-dunhams-gloriously-eccentric-style.html?mid=yahoostyle\"\u003E\u003Ci\u003ELena Dunham&#x2019;s Gloriously Eccentric Style\u003C\u002Fi\u003E\u003C\u002Fa\u003E\u003C\u002Fb\u003E\u003Cbr\u003E\u003C\u002Fp\u003E\n\u003Cp\u003E&#x201C;We want it to be an inclusive space,&#x201D; she said. &#x201C;We&#x2019;re not making any assumptions about your identity. We&#x2019;re making the assumption that you&#x2019;re passionate and you care about other people&#x2019;s emotions and style and you just want to live a more connected life.&#x201D;\u003C\u002Fp\u003E\n\u003Cp\u003EAnd though it&#x2019;s following in the footsteps of other celebrity lifestyle projects, don&#x2019;t call it Goop (Lenny will target the young and the broke, as opposed to the parental and the privileged) \u003Ci\u003Eor \u003C\u002Fi\u003Ethe anti-Goop.\u003C\u002Fp\u003E\n\u003Cp\u003E&#x201C;We don&#x2019;t see Lenny as the anti-Goop, even though we realize that our readers may not have the same income in their lives,&#x201D; Dunham said. Plus, Konner added, &#x201C;We worship Gwyneth. She has literally been the most supportive person of this project of anyone we&#x2019;ve spoken to.&#x201D;\u003C\u002Fp\u003E\n\u003Cp\u003E\u003Ci\u003E\u003Cb\u003EMore from \u003Ca
